<p><i><b>The Voice</b></i> is an American reality television singing competition broadcast on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>. Based on the original <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_of_Holland" title="The Voice of Holland">The Voice of Holland</a></i>, the concept of the series is to find currently unsigned singing talent (solo or duets, professional and amateur) contested by aspiring singers, age 13 or over,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> drawn from public auditions. The winner is determined by television viewers voting by telephone, Internet, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short_message_service" title="Short message service">SMS text</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> purchases of the audio-recorded artists' vocal performances. They receive US$100,000 and a <a href="/wiki/Recording_contract" title="Recording contract">record deal</a> with <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a> for winning the competition. The winners of the eleven seasons have been: <a href="/wiki/Javier_Colon" title="Javier Colon">Javier Colon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Paul" title="Jermaine Paul">Jermaine Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassadee_Pope" title="Cassadee Pope">Cassadee Pope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danielle_Bradbery" title="Danielle Bradbery">Danielle Bradbery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tessanne_Chin" title="Tessanne Chin">Tessanne Chin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josh_Kaufman" title="Josh Kaufman">Josh Kaufman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Wayne_Boyd" title="Craig Wayne Boyd">Craig Wayne Boyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sawyer_Fredericks" title="Sawyer Fredericks">Sawyer Fredericks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Smith_(musician)" title="Jordan Smith (musician)">Jordan Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alisan_Porter" title="Alisan Porter">Alisan Porter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Head" title="Sundance Head">Sundance Head</a>.</p>
<p>The series employs a panel of four coaches who critique the artists' performances and guide their teams of selected artists through the remainder of the season. They also compete to ensure that their act wins the competition, thus making them the winning coach. Members of the coaching panel include <a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a> (seasons 1-12), <a href="/wiki/Blake_Shelton" title="Blake Shelton">Blake Shelton</a> (seasons 1-12), <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a> (seasons 1–3, 5, 8, 10) <a href="/wiki/CeeLo_Green" title="CeeLo Green">CeeLo Green</a> (seasons 1–3, 5), <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> (season 4, 6), <a href="/wiki/Usher_(singer)" title="Usher (singer)">Usher</a> (season 4, 6), <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> (season 7, 9, 12), <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> (seasons 7–10) <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a> (season 11, 13) and <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> (seasons 11–12).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variety_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-variety-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Voice</i> began airing on April 26, 2011, as a spring TV season program. The show proved to be a hit for NBC and was subsequently expanded into the fall cycle when <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_3)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 3)">season three</a> premiered on September 10, 2012. The series premiered its eleventh season on September 19, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variety_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-variety-3">[3]</a></sup> On October 18, 2016, NBC renewed the series through its thirteenth season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline.com_10182016_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline.com_10182016-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#The_Voice_Live_on_Tour"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext"><i>The Voice</i> Live on Tour</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Video_game"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Video game</span></a></li>

</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conception">Conception</span></h2>
<p>An adaptation of the Dutch show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_of_Holland" title="The Voice of Holland">The Voice of Holland</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> announced the show under the name <i>The Voice of America</i> in December 2010;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> its name was soon shortened to <i>The Voice</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbc-news_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbc-news-6">[6]</a></sup> In each season, the winner receives $100,000 and a record deal with <a href="/wiki/Universal_Republic_Records" title="Universal Republic Records">Universal Republic Records</a> (seasons 1 &amp; 2), <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a> (season 3–present).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Selection_process_and_format">Selection process and format</span></h2>
<p>Each season begins with the "Blind Auditions," where coaches form their team of artists (8 in season 1, 12 in seasons 2 and 4–11, and 16 in season 3) whom they mentor through the remainder of the season. The coaches' chairs are faced towards the audience during artists' performances; those interested in an artist press their button, which turns their chair towards the artist and illuminates the bottom of the chair to read "I want you." At the conclusion of the performance, an artist either defaults to the only coach who turned around, or selects his or her coach if more than one coach expresses interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Format_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Format-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the "Battle Rounds," each coach pairs two of his or her team members to perform together, then chooses one to advance in the competition. In each season, coaches are assisted by celebrity mentors that are different each season. A new element was added in <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_3)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 3)">season three</a>; coaches were given two "steals", allowing each coach to select two individuals who were eliminated during a battle round by another coach.</p>
<p>The Knockout Rounds were also introduced in season three. A pair of artists within a team are selected to sing individual performances in succession. They are not told until a few minutes prior to their performances who their partner is. The artists get to choose their own songs in this round, although they continue to get help and advice from their respective coaches. At the conclusion of the performances, coaches would decide which one of each pair gets to advance to the next round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Format_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Format-7">[7]</a></sup> Just like in the battle rounds, the coaches can steal one eliminated artist from another coach starting with <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_5)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 5)">season five</a>.</p>
<p>The "Battles, Round 2" were introduced to replace the Knockout Rounds in <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_6)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 6)">season six</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Format_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Format-7">[7]</a></sup> Similar to the Knockout Rounds, each singer is paired randomly within their team. One celebrity key adviser also assists all four of the coaches and their teams in preparation of these rounds. Coaches give each Battle pairing a list of songs and each pair must agree on which song to sing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Each coach can still decide which of their singers in each pair will advance to the next round. The coaches are also allowed one steal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> However, the Knockouts were brought back in season seven.</p>
<p>In the final live performance phase of the competition, artists perform in weekly shows, where public voting narrows to a final group of artists and eventually declares a winner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Format_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Format-7">[7]</a></sup> The coaches have the power to save one artist that had not received the public's vote that week. As of season two, these artists would give a last chance performance to win their coach's save. However, in deciding who moves on to the final four phase, the television audience and the coaches have equal say. With one team member remaining for each coach, the contestants compete against each other in the finale, where the outcome is decided solely by public vote. In the first two seasons, one contestant from each team would advance to the final four. Due to the possibility of having multiple potential winners on the same team, eliminations were adjusted in season three to eliminate contestants who earned the lowest number of votes, thus not guaranteeing a coach and a contestant in the (reduced) final three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voting_system">Voting system</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._TV_series)_discography" title="The Voice (U.S. TV series) discography">The Voice (U.S. TV series) discography</a></div>
<p>In a first for a music competition series, NBC and <a href="/wiki/Universal_Republic_Records" title="Universal Republic Records">Universal Republic Records</a> offered fans of the show the ability to vote for their favorite artists by purchasing the studio versions of the songs that they perform on the live show each week via the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>. Alternative methods of voting can be done through toll-free phone calls (until 2015), text messaging (provided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sprint_Nextel" title="Sprint Nextel">Sprint</a> (until 2015)), the show's app, and through online votes via NBC.com and <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>. Each method is limited to ten votes per user. Voting lasts until noon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Standard_Time_(North_America)" title="Eastern Standard Time (North America)">EST</a> the next day.</p>
<p>As of the top 12 results show of season three, producers made changes in the voting system with regards to iTunes singles purchases. Previous voting via iTunes purchases of contestant performances had previously only counted singly during the official voting window and only accredited to the live show in concern. If a competitor's performance charts within the Top 10 of the iTunes "Top 200 Singles Chart" during this window, it will be given an iTunes bonus that multiplies iTunes votes made by ten. Starting in season five, the iTunes bonus multiplier is now five for the studio versions of the songs performed by the competitors. The finale's vote count will include a 'Cumulative iTunes Vote Total' of all singles (from top 12 onwards) purchased during and outside of the various voting windows, with iTunes bonuses previously earned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Only the studio recording of the contestants' performances, not the live performance, are available on iTunes. In the first season, the battle rounds were recorded in the studio with both artists in the pairing. However, from season two on, only the winner's version of the song from the battle round is released. Season seven reverted to the old style of both artists. With the introduction of the Knockout Rounds in season three, where each contestant sang a separate song, only the winner's single is released.</p>
<p>The "Instant Save" was introduced in season five. During the live elimination episodes, viewers are given a five-minute window to vote for the contestants in danger of elimination by using their <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> account to decide which contestant will move on to the next show, starting with the Top 12. Home viewers can only vote once per account for one contestant of their choice.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaches_and_hosts">Coaches and hosts</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_Lady_Michelle_Obama_and_Dr._Jill_Biden_record_social_media_videos_with_Adam_Levine_and_Blake_Shelton_prior_to_the_kick_off_of_the_5th_anniversary_of_their_Joining_Forces_initiative_on_NBC%27s_The_Voice.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="654" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/First_Lady_Michelle_Obama_and_Dr._Jill_Biden_record_social_media_videos_with_Adam_Levine_and_Blake_Shelton_prior_to_the_kick_off_of_the_5th_anniversary_of_their_Joining_Forces_initiative_on_NBC%27s_The_Voice.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/First_Lady_Michelle_Obama_and_Dr._Jill_Biden_record_social_media_videos_with_Adam_Levine_and_Blake_Shelton_prior_to_the_kick_off_of_the_5th_anniversary_of_their_Joining_Forces_initiative_on_NBC%27s_The_Voice.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/First_Lady_Michelle_Obama_and_Dr._Jill_Biden_record_social_media_videos_with_Adam_Levine_and_Blake_Shelton_prior_to_the_kick_off_of_the_5th_anniversary_of_their_Joining_Forces_initiative_on_NBC%27s_The_Voice.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_Lady_Michelle_Obama_and_Dr._Jill_Biden_record_social_media_videos_with_Adam_Levine_and_Blake_Shelton_prior_to_the_kick_off_of_the_5th_anniversary_of_their_Joining_Forces_initiative_on_NBC%27s_The_Voice.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Lady_Michelle_Obama" title="First Lady Michelle Obama">First Lady Michelle Obama</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr._Jill_Biden" title="Dr. Jill Biden">Dr. Jill Biden</a> record social media videos with Adam Levine and Blake Shelton prior to the kick-off of the 5th anniversary of their Joining Forces initiative, May 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/CeeLo_Green" title="CeeLo Green">CeeLo Green</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gnarls_Barkley" title="Gnarls Barkley">Gnarls Barkley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a> became the first confirmed coaches in February 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Blake_Shelton" title="Blake Shelton">Blake Shelton</a> in March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Aguilera and Green did not return for season four and were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> as substitute coaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Aguilera and Green then returned for season five, while Shakira and Usher returned for season six.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> in February 2014, Green revealed that he would not be returning to <i>The Voice</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> On March 31, 2014, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> would become Green's replacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pharrell_season_7_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-pharrell_season_7-19">[19]</a></sup> On April 19, 2014, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/No_Doubt" title="No Doubt">No Doubt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stefani" title="Gwen Stefani">Gwen Stefani</a> would replace Aguilera in season seven due to her pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stefani_7_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stefani_7-20">[20]</a></sup> On May 20, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> confirmed that after season six, they would focus on their music. However, they did not eliminate the possibility of returning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> On March 25, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a> confirmed that following her role as key advisor during the tenth season that she would be joining the series once again in its eleventh season as a coach, replacing <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> That same day, <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> was also announced to be joining the series as a coach for the eleventh season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> On October 18, 2016, it was announced that Stefani would re-join the coaches' panel for the series' twelfth season, alongside returning coaches Keys, Levine and Shelton; it was also confirmed that Cyrus would return for the thirteenth season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline.com_10182016_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline.com_10182016-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carson_Daly" title="Carson Daly">Carson Daly</a> has hosted the series since the inaugural season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carson_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-carson-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alison_Haislip" title="Alison Haislip">Alison Haislip</a> served as the original "backstage, online and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_networking" title="Social networking">social media</a> correspondent"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haislip_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-haislip-25">[25]</a></sup> and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Christina_Milian" title="Christina Milian">Christina Milian</a>. Milian did not return for season five, at which point Daly assumed her duties as the social media correspondent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Milian_not_returning_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Milian_not_returning-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KTLA.2C_Milian_no_longer_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-KTLA.2C_Milian_no_longer-27">[27]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaches.27_advisors">Coaches' advisors</span></h2>

<tr>
<th colspan="6">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^1</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 10 performances, Cee Lo Green, Christina Aguilera and Blake Shelton brought in Jennifer Hudson, Ron Fair and Scott Hendricks respectively to help them coach their teams.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_2"><b><a href="#ref_2">^2</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 8 performances, Cee Lo Green brought in Bill Withers to help coach his contestant <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_David" title="Nicholas David">Nicholas David</a> on his performance of "<a href="/wiki/Lean_on_Me_(song)" title="Lean on Me (song)">Lean on Me</a>".</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_3"><b><a href="#ref_3">^3</a></b></span> Due to being sick during the rehearsals of the Top 6, Cee Lo Green brought in Pat Monahan to coach his team for the week. Green did however pick the songs which his team members would sing that week and kept in touch with them by phone.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_4"><b><a href="#ref_4">^4</a></b></span> The mentors of the Battle Rounds reprised their roles during the week of the Top 10 performances except Joel Madden who was working on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Voice_(Australia)" title="The Voice (Australia)"><i>The Voice</i> in Australia</a>. Shakira instead brought in Cee Lo Green to help coach her team that week.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_5"><b><a href="#ref_5">^5</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 12 performances, Usher brought in his choreographer Aakomon Jones to help coach his team.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_6"><b><a href="#ref_6">^6</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 6 performances, Taylor Swift attended <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Chamuel" title="Michelle Chamuel">Michelle Chamuel</a>'s rehearsal of "<a href="/wiki/I_Knew_You_Were_Trouble" title="I Knew You Were Trouble">I Knew You Were Trouble</a>".</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_7"><b><a href="#ref_7">^7</a></b></span> With the replacement of the Knockout Rounds with the "Battles, Round 2" in season 6, <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> frontman Chris Martin served as the sole advisor for every team.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_8"><b><a href="#ref_8">^8</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 10 performances, all four coaches brought advisors to help coach their teams. Graham Nash helped Team Adam, busbee helped Team Shakira, Natural helped Team Usher, and Scott Hendricks helped Team Blake.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_9"><b><a href="#ref_9">^9</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 8 performances, Adam Levine brought in fellow <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">band member</a> James Valentine and Blake Shelton brought in former <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_2)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 2)">season two</a> contestant Gwen Sebastian to help coach their teams.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_10"><b><a href="#ref_10">^10</a></b></span> With the return of the Knockout Rounds in season seven, Taylor Swift served as the sole advisor for every team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_11"><b><a href="#ref_11">^11</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 10 performances, all four coaches brought advisors to help coach their teams.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_12"><b><a href="#ref_12">^12</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 12 performances, Reba McEntire help all four coaches coaching the teams.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_13"><b><a href="#ref_13">^13</a></b></span> During the week of the Top 10 performances, all four coaches brought advisors to help coach their teams. Dave Stewart helped Team Adam, Ryan Tedder helped Team Pharrell, Mark Ronson helped Team Christina, and Scott Hendricks helped Team Blake.</td>
</tr>
</table>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_synopses">Season synopses</span></h2>
<p>Names in bold type indicate the winner of the season.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_1">Season 1</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_1)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 1)">The Voice (U.S. season 1)</a></div>
<p>The first season of <i>The Voice</i> premiered on April 26, 2011, and concluded on June 29. The coaching panel consisted of <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cee_Lo_Green" title="Cee Lo Green">Cee Lo Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Levine" title="Adam Levine">Adam Levine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blake_Shelton" title="Blake Shelton">Blake Shelton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carson_Daly" title="Carson Daly">Carson Daly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alison_Haislip" title="Alison Haislip">Alison Haislip</a> respectively appeared as the host and social media correspondent. Contestant auditions were held in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nashville" title="Nashville">Nashville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> during January and February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>It delivered the highest 18–49 rating for a series premiere on a major broadcast network since <i><a href="/wiki/Undercover_Boss" title="Undercover Boss">Undercover Boss</a></i> debuted after the Super Bowl in February 2010. It became the first new primetime series of the season (from ABC, CBS, NBC, or Fox) to increase in adults 18–49 and total viewers from its first week to its second. Owing to the strong performance of the show, NBC offered expanded two-hour live episodes beginning June 7, following <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Got_Talent" title="America's Got Talent">America's Got Talent</a></i>, with an additional results show.</p>
<p>Each coach was allowed to advance four top to the live shows:</p>

<td bgcolor="#D0F0C0" scope="col" style="width:13%;"><b><span class="nowrap">Team Adam</span></b></td>

<p>Four finalists were advanced to the final round. Javier Colon was announced as the winner of the season, while Dia Frampton was declared the runner-up. Third and fourth places were a draw between Vicci Martinez and Beverly McClellan.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_2">Season 2</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_2)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 2)">The Voice (U.S. season 2)</a></div>
<p>Season two premiered on February 5, 2012 as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Super_Bowl_lead-out_programs" title="List of Super Bowl lead-out programs">lead-out program</a> after <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a>; it concluded on May 8. The original coaching panel remained intact, while Haislip was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Christina_Milian" title="Christina Milian">Christina Milian</a> as the social media correspondent. Its regular time slot held a 6.7 rating, 17 share in adults 18–49, 17.8 million viewers overall and winning every half-hour in adults 18–49, adults 18–34, adults 25–54 and total viewers versus first-run competition on ABC, CBS, Fox and CW. The shows' continued premiere on Monday delivered NBC's highest 18–49 rating in this time period, excluding Olympics, in nearly eight years (since February 16, 2004) and the network's biggest overall non-Olympic viewership in the slot since January 15, 2007. That season, <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">Kia Motors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Corporation" title="Sprint Corporation">Sprint</a> and <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> became the official sponsors of <i>The Voice</i>.</p>
<p>Each coach was allowed to advance six top to the live shows:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_4">Season 4</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._season_4)" title="The Voice (U.S. season 4)">The Voice (U.S. season 4)</a></div>
<p>Season four premiered on March 25, 2013, and concluded on June 18. The coaching panel was modified for the first time in the series' history, with <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> replacing Aguilera and Green during their hiatuses from the program. Daly and Milian continued appearing for their respective positions. 13.64 million viewers tuned in, up from last season by 1.36 million viewers.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_12">Season 12</span></h3>
<p>Season twelve will premiere on February 27, 2017<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> with Gwen Stefani and Alicia Keys returning as coaches alongside Levine and Shelton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline.com_10182016_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline.com_10182016-4">[4]</a></sup> Cyrus will be taking a break from the show; however, she will return as coach on the show's thirteenth season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deadline.com_10182016_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline.com_10182016-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Voz_Kids"><i>La Voz Kids</i></span></h2>
<p>In 2013, American Spanish-language network <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">Telemundo</a> (a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal_Television_Group" title="NBCUniversal Television Group">NBCUniversal Television Group</a>) introduced a children's version of <i>The Voice</i> in Spanish called <i>La Voz Kids</i>. It featured Spanish-speaking American children from 7 to 15 years of age. Prizes include $50,000 cash for their education and a recording contract with Universal Music Group. The show debuted on May 5, 2013, and is hosted by Jorge Bernal (from <i>¡Suelta La Sopa!</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Daisy_Fuentes" title="Daisy Fuentes">Daisy Fuentes</a>. The coaches in season one were <a href="/wiki/Prince_Royce" title="Prince Royce">Prince Royce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paulina_Rubio" title="Paulina Rubio">Paulina Rubio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Tapia" title="Roberto Tapia">Roberto Tapia</a>. The first season aired 13 episodes with the season finale airing on July 28, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Season two saw <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Natalia Jiménez">Natalia Jiménez</a> replace Paulina Rubio as one of the coaches. The other coaches and hosts remained the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the show's third season, <a href="/wiki/Daddy_Yankee" title="Daddy Yankee">Daddy Yankee</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandez" title="Pedro Fernandez">Pedro Fernandez</a> took Tapia and Royce's place as the new coaches along with season two veteran Natalia Jiménez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>At their 2015 <a href="/wiki/Upfront_(advertising)" title="Upfront (advertising)">Upfronts</a>, Telemundo announced that La Voz Kids would return for a fourth season, with all three Season 3 coaches returning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>
<p>In 2016, a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> study of the 50 TV shows with the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Facebook_Like" title="Facebook Like">Facebook Likes</a> found that <i>The Voice</i> "is most popular in North Dakota and least popular in New York. It was behind only <i><a href="/wiki/Duck_Dynasty" title="Duck Dynasty">Duck Dynasty</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Fast_N%27_Loud" title="Fast N' Loud">Fast N' Loud</a></i> in its correlation with <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">Trump voters</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katz20161227_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-katz20161227-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_The_Voice_(U.S._TV_series)" title="List of awards and nominations received by The Voice (U.S. TV series)">List of awards and nominations received by The Voice (U.S. TV series)</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ratings">Ratings</span></h3>
<p>The first season premiered strong at 11.78 million viewers, and actually grew upon that audience through its first season. In the 18–49 demographic, the show constantly found itself in the top 5. For its average season rating, the show landed itself as No. 20 with total viewers at nearly 12 million viewers. In the 18–49 rankings, the show was No. 4 at a 5.4 ranking.</p>
<p>The second season premiered on <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl</a> Sunday, February 5, 2012, and for a while managed to keep a 6.0 in the adults 18–49 demographic and 17 million viewers. Partnering <i>The Voice</i> with <i><a href="/wiki/Smash_(TV_series)" title="Smash (TV series)">Smash</a></i> (NBC's musical drama) helped NBC win the Monday night ratings. However, by Monday, April 9, the ratings had fallen to a 4.0 rating in the adult 18–49 demographic.</p>
<p>The third season premiered on Monday, September 10, 2012 to 12.28 million viewers and a 4.2 rating in the 18–49 demographic and has since then grown to a season high 4.8 rating in the 18–49 demographic on October 8, October 15 and 29, 2012 and a 4.9 rating in the finale. <i>The Voice</i>, along with NBC's new drama, <i><a href="/wiki/Revolution_(TV_series)" title="Revolution (TV series)">Revolution</a></i> has once again led NBC to win every Monday night of the season so far, just like it did last season. On Tuesdays, comedies <i><a href="/wiki/Go_On_(TV_series)" title="Go On (TV series)">Go On</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Normal_(TV_series)" title="The New Normal (TV series)">The New Normal</a></i> have been successful thanks to <i>The Voice</i>, leading NBC to be the only network of the <i>Big 5</i> to grow in ratings from last season.</p>
<p>The fourth season premiered on Monday, March 25, 2013 to a 13.64 million viewer audience, scoring a 4.8 in the 18–49 demographic but fell back to a 12.41 million viewer audience. In the 18–49 demographic, this first episode had a 4.1 score.</p>
<p>The fifth season premiered on Monday, September 23, 2013 scoring 14.98 million viewers and a 5.1 in the 18–49 demographic.</p>
<p>The sixth season premiered on February 24, 2014 and was watched by 15.74 million viewers with a 4.7 rating in the 18–49 demographic. It was up from last season's premiere by .76 million viewers.</p>
<p>The seventh season premiered on September 22, 2014 and was watched by 12.95 million viewers with a 3.9 rating in the 18–49 demographic. It was down from last season's premiere by 2.91 million viewers.</p>
<p>The eighth season premiered on February 23, 2015, and was watched by 13.97 million viewers with a 4.1 rating in the 18–49 demographic. It was up from last season's premiere by 1.02 million viewers.</p>
<p>The ninth season premiered on September 21, 2015, and was watched by 12.37 million viewers with a 3.5 rating in the 18–49 demographic. It was down from last falls premiere by .48 million viewers.</p>
<p>The tenth season premiered on February 29, 2016, and was watched by 13.33 million viewers with a 3.4 rating in the 18–49 demographic. It was up from last season's premiere by .96 million viewers.</p>
<p>The eleventh season premiered on September 19, 2016, and was watched by 12.10 million viewers with a 3.3 rating in the 18–49 demographic. It is down from last season's premiere by 1.23 million viewers.</p>
<dl>
<dd><i>Each U.S. network television season starts in late September and ends in late May, which coincides with the completion of May <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweeps" title="Sweeps">sweeps</a>.</i></dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Voice_Live_on_Tour"><i>The Voice</i> Live on Tour</span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">

<td class="mbox-image">

<p>In the final episode of the first season, Carson Daly announced a summer concert tour. This tour had six stops across the United States, including Los Angeles, Las Vegas, Chicago, Boston, Wallingford, and New York. The tour featured the top two finalists from each team, including Javier Colon, Dia Frampton, Vicci Martinez, Beverly McClellan, Xenia, Frenchie Davis, Nakia, and Casey Weston. Out of the six dates, the New York show was a sell-out. However, as overall ticket sales were lackluster, the tour was canceled in subsequent seasons. In 2014, the tour was resumed from June 21, 2014 to August 2, 2014, including the contestants of seasons five and six, and season one contestant Dia Frampton.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_game">Video game</span></h2>
<p><i>The Voice: I Want You</i> is a video game based on the television show releasing on <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a> on October 21, 2014 published by <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>. The game includes a microphone and it has songs from the show including songs performed by the coaches.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast">Broadcast</span></h2>
<p>The show premiered in Canada on April 26, 2011 on <a href="/wiki/CTV_Television_Network" title="CTV Television Network">CTV</a>. In Asia, the series aired on August 21, 2011 on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AXN_Asia" title="AXN Asia">AXN</a>, but later moves in <a href="/wiki/Star_World" title="Star World">Star World</a> starting Season 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philstar_1_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Philstar_1-99">[99]</a></sup> It premiered in New Zealand on July 16, 2011 on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TV2_(New_Zealand)" title="TV2 (New Zealand)">TV2</a>, in Australia on August 9, 2011 on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Go!_(Australian_TV_channel)" title="Go! (Australian TV channel)">Go!</a>, in South Africa on October 5, 2011 on <a href="/wiki/SABC_3" title="SABC 3">SABC 3</a>, and on March 31, 2012 in the Philippines on <a href="/wiki/Studio_23" title="Studio 23">Studio 23</a> (now <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Abs-cbn_sports%2BAction&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Abs-cbn sports+Action (page does not exist)">abs-cbn sports+Action</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lopez_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lopez-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
